Why is it important to scroll through the planes?  The scrolling feature of this software is unique for pinpointing structures and understanding relationships of structures to one another. Understanding where you are in these planes is key to understanding your patient's anatomy.  2.  Why is it helpful to see all or some of the planes in the 3D window as you scroll?  This unique feature actually helps you pinpoint the structure on the 3D cadaver and works whether the cadaver is whole or sectioned, for better visualization. supplied by the superior gluteal nerve.  Now, lets add muscles that will form the posterior compartment of the thigh:  Add in the semimembranosus  Add in the semitendinosus  Note how the semitendinosus is a long tendon inferiorly whereas the semimembranosus is more muscular inferiorly. Add in the biceps femoris  Note that the biceps femoris has 2 heads. The long head attaches superiorly to the ischial tuberosity, whereas the short head attaches superiorly to the lateral lip of the linea aspera between the adductor magnus and vastus lateralis. The muscles that attach to the ischial tuberosity (semimembranosus, semitendinosus and long head of biceps) are medially placed and supplied by the tibial portion of the sciatic nerve. The short head of biceps is more laterally placed and is supplied by the common fibular portion of the sciatic nerve. ","roles":{"textData":{}}},{"id":"Text_Caption_629","class":"TODO::Senthil","instance":"Text_Caption_629","title":"Respiration (inspiration/ expiration) is accomplished by the following muscles:  Add the diaphragm which descends as it contracts and creates negative pressure  Add the internal intercostal  muscles If you rotate the 3D model, note that these muscles are muscular anteriorly and aponeurotic posteriorly.  Add the external intercostal muscles If you rotate the 3D model, note that these muscles are muscular posteriorly and aponeurotic anteriorly.  The innermost intercostals complete the three intercostal muscles and are the deepest of the three. These muscles are muscular for 3/4 of the intercostal space and are aponeurotic anteriorly and posteriorly. They are not visible in the 3D model.   The intercostal muscles contract and stiffen the rib cage to counter negative pressure, along with lifting and rotating ribs 2 through 10 to increase the thoracic volume.  Think of the movement of the intercostal muscles as a combination of a pump lever and a bucket handle maneuver to increase thoracic volume.  The lungs passively inflate during this part of the cycle. The letter a- (preceding – zygos in this case) is known as alpha privative; it expresses negation or that which is not.
